immunogam belongs to a group of medicines called immunoglobulins ( antibodies ) that are used to treat certain infections in your blood . immunogam is used to increase levels of human hepatitis b immune cells ( e . g , igg ) in the blood plasma of screened patients . this is because immunogam can be used to prevent the spread of histiococcus b virus in haemodialysed patients who have not been vaccinated with a hepb virus carrier . it is used in combination with an immune response , which results in measurable levels of hispb antibodies . vaccination is a method of continuous prevention for patients infected with hepatisb .
immunogam may cause an allergic reaction to human immunoglobulins or other blood products . if you have an iga deficiency , you may have an allergy reaction to iga containing products ( see section 18 ). warnings and precautions talk to your doctor , pharmacist or nurse before taking immunogam . allergic reactions may include chills , headache , fever , vomiting , allergic reactions , such as nausea , arthralgia , joint pain , low blood pressure , moderate low back pain . immunogam is used in combination with antibodies to hepatitis b immunisin regularly , which are used in humans . in adults , immunogam has been used in children and adolescents aged 18 years of age . it is not known whether immunogam can cause adverse reactions such as chills or headache . these may be signs of fever or vomiting .
immunogam is used to prevent the spread of hepatitis b virus . the first vaccine dose is a human - based immunoglobulin ( hbi ) vaccine . administration prevention : the recommended dose is 500 mg / ml . in haemodialysed patients , 500 mg is given twice a day for 24 hours and 72 hours . if you are not sure , talk to your doctor or pharmacist . seroconversion is the first step in the process of vaccination . you will be given immunogam at the same time each day . your doctor will decide whether or not to give you immunogam . it is important that you do not have to take more immunogam than you should . immunogam should not be given in combination with other medicines . this is because immunogam does not affect the immune system of your body .
like all medicines , immunogam can cause side effects , although not everybody gets them . the most common side effects are : very common ( may affect more than 1 in 10 people ) nausea , fatigue , induration , swelling . if you experience any of the following side effects after taking immunogam , talk to your doctor or pharmacist . this includes any possible side effects not listed in this leaflet . you can also report side effects directly via the national reporting system listed in section 6 . reporting of side effects you can help provide more information on the safety of immunogam ( see section " warnings and precautions "). most of the side effects may affect up to 1 in 100 people . not all patients are treated with 10 to 1 , 000 people , and undesirable effects may occur during clinical trials . immunogam is used in the treatment of muscle . it is used to treat nausea and fatigue .
keep this medicine out of the sight and reach of children . do not use immunogam after the expiry date which is stated on the carton and the blister after exp . if you notice that immunogam is cloudy or has deposits , ask your pharmacist how to dispose of medicines you no longer use . these measures will help to protect the environment .
what immunogam contains the active substance is human hepatitis b immunoglobulin . each vial contains 1 mg of immunogam and 5 mg of human plasma protein ( 96 ). the other ingredients are polysorbate 80 and water for injection . the pack immunogam is a solution for injection in a glass vial with a pale yellow liquid . it is available in packs of 1 vial .

remicade is used to treat rheumatoid arthritis . it is given to patients with 3 kg body weight . if you have psoriatic arthritis , ankylosing spondylitis ( bechterew ' s disease ) if your doctor tells you that you are not sure , talk to your doctor , pharmacist or nurse . your doctor will tell you how much you need to take and how much to take . the recommended dose is 5 mg / ml , depending on your bodyweight . you will be given the medicine as an infusion ( drip ) over 2 hours in the veins of your arm . during the third treatment , you will receive the medicine over a period of over two hours . this is because the medicine is given over two weeks .
like all medicines , this medicine can cause side effects , although not everybody gets them . the most common side effects are mild to moderate . serious side effects may occur during treatment . tell your doctor immediately if you notice any of the following side effects after your treatment with remicade : - you have an allergic reaction , such as swelling of your face , lips , mouth or throat , difficulty in swallowing or breathing , skin rash , hives or swelling of the hands , feet or ankles . these reactions may be signs of an allergy reaction . see section 2 for more information on allergic reactions . you can also report side effects directly via the national reporting system listed in appendix v . this includes any possible side effects not listed in this leaflet . warnings and precautions talk to your doctor , pharmacist or nurse as soon as possible . your doctor will
keep this medicine out of the sight and reach of children . do not use this medicine after the expiry date which is stated on the label and carton after exp . the expiration date refers to the last day of that month . store in a refrigerator ( 2 - 8 ). do not freeze . this medicine does not require any special storage conditions . remicade can be stored in the original package in order to protect from light . after infusion , it should be stored at room temperature for at least 3 hours . it should not be used in combination with food , drink or household waste . ask your pharmacist how to dispose of medicines you no longer use . these measures will help protect the environment .

mirvaso contains the active substance brimonidine , which belongs to a group of medicines called alpha agonists . it is used to treat the appearance of redness in the face caused by rosacea . redness of the face is a sign of high levels of blood flow in the facial skin , resulting in enlargement ( dilatation ) of the small blood vessels of the skin . mirvao acts by blocking the flow of blood vessels and reducing the excess blood flow . this reduces redness .
do not take mirvaso - if you are allergic to brimonidine or any of the other ingredients of this medicine ( listed in section 6 ). warnings and precautions talk to your doctor , pharmacist or nurse before you are given this medicine . tell your doctor or pharmacist if your child is more than 6 years of age or older . side effects of the medicine may occur under the skin . certain medicines used to treat depression ( parkinson ' s disease ) include monoamine oxidase ( mao ) inhibitors such as selegiline , moclobemide , tricyclic antidepressants ( imipramine ), tetracyclic antidepressants such as maprotiline, mianserin and mirtazapin . if any of these medicines are not available , ask your doctor for advice . do not use mirvas

tecartus is a gene therapy medicine used to treat mantle cell lymphoma . it is used in combination with other medicines to treat refractory mastectomy . your own white blood cells are called autologous anti - cd19 - transduced CD3+ cells ( a type of cancer that affects the immune system ). it is produced by b - lymphocytes , which are produced in the body in an uncontrolled way in which they are not able to grow in the lymph tissue ( e . g . bone marrow ) in the blood , where they are unable to grow , so that they cannot grow in your blood . this causes the cancer cells to grow more and more in your body , causing them to grow faster than normal . in this way , the tumour cells can grow faster and faster .
always take this medicine exactly as your doctor has told you . check with your doctor or pharmacist if you are allergic to this medicine or any of the other ingredients of this medicine ( listed in section 6 ). warnings and precautions talk to your doctor , pharmacist or nurse before you are given tecartus . the medicine contains white blood cells . your doctor will check your blood ( lymphodepleting chemotherapy ) every 3 months . you will be given the medicine for autologous use . tests , checks and checks of your lungs , heart , kidney , blood pressure , infection , inflammation , your cancer , graft - versus - host disease , or a transplant , you will have symptoms such as rash , nausea , and vomiting . if your doctor tells you to stop taking the medicine , tell your doctor as soon as possible .
tecartus is used to treat your own white blood cells . your cells are injected into a catheter placed in a vein . a procedure called leukapheresis is performed to remove the cells from your blood . you will be given a dose of 3 to 6 ml of your blood per day . this will be followed by a period of 2 to 3 weeks . the amount of your white blood cell count will be monitored by your doctor , pharmacist or nurse . medicines used during the course of treatment , lymphodepleting chemotherapy , which is a process of removing the damaged cells from the body for 30 to 60 days . other medicines used for infusion reactions such as fever . these other medicines are not recommended for use in children and adolescents .
like all medicines , this medicine can cause side effects , although not everybody gets them . tell your doctor straight away if you notice any of the side effects listed in section 6 . warnings and precautions talk to your doctor , pharmacist or nurse immediately . the following side effects may occur after the tecartus infusion : common ( may affect more than 1 in 10 people ): fever , chills , reduced blood pressure , symptoms include dizziness , lightheadedness and fluid in the lungs . all symptoms may be signs of a condition called cytokine release syndrome ( loss of consciousness or decreased level of consciousness , confusion , memory loss ). if any of these occur , ask your doctor or pharmacist . this includes any possible side effects not listed in this leaflet . you can also report side effects directly via the national reporting system listed in appendix v

duoplavin contains the active substance clopidogrel , acetylsalicylic acid ( asa ). it belongs to a group of medicines called antiplatelet medicinal products . platelets are very small structures in the blood , which can cause blood clotting . this clumping occurs in blood vessels , and can lead to the formation of antibodies against these clots . atherothrombosis is a type of thrombotic disorder in which the drug is used , it is used to reduce the risk of a person who has hardened arteries . it is also used in patients who have suffered atherosclerotic events , such as stroke , heart attack , or death .

atripla contains three active substances that are used to treat human immunodeficiency virus ( hiv ) infection : efavirenz , a non - nucleoside reverse transcriptase inhibitor ( nnrti ), emtricitabine , which is a nuclear-nucleic acid - induced transcription factor , and tenofovir . these active substances are used in combination with antiretroviral medicines . they are used for the treatment of the virus . atripl is used as a treatment for the human immune deficit virus , or hiv ( infection ) in adults and children aged 18 years and older . it is also used in children and adolescents of all ages . this is because there is no evidence of hiv infection .

like all medicines , this medicine can cause side effects , although not everybody gets them . warnings and precautions talk to your doctor or pharmacist if you notice any of the following side effects while taking palforzia : severe allergic reactions . the reaction may include trouble breathing , throat tightness , feeling offulness , trouble swallowing , speaking - changes in voice , dizziness - fainting - severe stomach cramps , pain , vomiting - diarrhoea , severe flushing or itching of the skin palforizia may cause problems with the stomach and digestive system . if any of these occur , tell your doctor immediately . this includes any possible side effects not listed in this leaflet . you can also report side effects directly via the national reporting system listed in appendix v .

what zerene contains - the active substance is benzodiazepine . it belongs to a group of medicinal products called hypnotic actions . - it is used to treat sleeping problems after treatment . treatment should be stopped if you have problems sleeping .
